25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25922-1" target="أَضْلَلْتُهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (IB, TA,) which means <hi rend="ital">I lost it, and knew not its place;</hi> meaning, for instance, a horse, or she-camel, or the like: (Az, Msb:) [thus] one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَضْلَلْتُ بِعِيرِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I lost my camel, and knew not his place,</hi>] (AA, ISk, S, IB, O) when his shank has been tied up to his arm and one does not find the way to him, and when he has been left loose and has gone away whither one knows not: (AA, IB, TA:) but Yoo differs from others respecting this case; for, accord. to him, one says, <foreign lang="ar">اضلّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ بَعِيرَهُ</foreign> and also <foreign lang="ar">ضَلَّهُ</foreign>, in the same sense; (O, TA;) and the like is said in the K: (TA:) and it is also said in the Bári' that when you seek an animal and miss its place and find not the way to it, it is regarded as in the category of stationary things, and therefore you say <foreign lang="ar">ضَلِلْتُهُ</foreign>. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَلَّ</foreign> signifies also <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, confounded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">perplexed, and unable to see his right course.</hi> (Ibn-Es-Seed, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also, aor.

                  <form>       
                     <itype>4</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">اضلّهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِضْلَالٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, made him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused him, to err, stray,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">go astray; to deviate from the right way</hi> or <hi rend="ital">course,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from that which was right; to miss,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lose, the right way;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to lose his way.</hi> (Az, TA.) [See also 2, first sentence.] <foreign lang="ar">الإِضْلَالُ</foreign> is of two sorts: one of these is the consequence of erring, or straying; either as in the case in which one says <foreign lang="ar">أَضْلَلْتُ البَعِيرَ</foreign> (expl. above, see 1, former half); or the decreeing that one shall err, or stray, &amp;c., because he has done so already, and this is sometimes the case when the <foreign lang="ar">إِضْلَال</foreign> of a man is attributed to God: the other sort is the embellishing [or commending] to a man that which is false, or wrong, or vain, in order that he may err, or stray, &amp;c.: and God's <foreign lang="ar">إِضْلَال</foreign> of a man is of two sorts; one of which has been expl. above; the other is God's so constituting man that when he observes [and pursues] a certain course, or way, [of acting or the like], whether it be such as is commended or such as is discommended, he habituates himself to it, and esteems it pleasant, and keeps to it, and finds it difficult to turn from it, wherefore it is said that custom is a second nature. (Er-Rághib, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, made,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, to perish,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">become lost;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلَكَهُ</foreign>, (S, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَضَاعَهُ</foreign>, (El-Fárábee, S, O, Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">ضَيَّعَهُ</foreign>; (TA;) [<foreign lang="ar">اضاعهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ضيّعهُ</foreign> signifying the same; and so <foreign lang="ar">اضلّهُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25924-1" target="ضللّٰهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; whence,] <foreign lang="ar">أَلَمْ يَجْعَلْ كَيْدَهُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى تَضْلِيلٍ</foreign>, in the Kur cv. 2, means [<hi rend="ital">Did He not make their plot to be</hi> such as ended] <hi rend="ital">in a causing to perish,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">become lost,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">فِى تَضْيِيعٍ</foreign>,) and <hi rend="ital">in annulment?</hi> (Ksh, Bd.) <foreign lang="ar">أَضَلَّ أَعْمَالَهُمْ</foreign>, in the Kur [xlvii. 1 and 9, which may be rendered <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He will cause their works to be lost,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to be of no effect</hi>], means, accord. to Aboo-Is-hák, <hi rend="ital">He will not recompense them for their</hi> good <hi rend="ital">works;</hi> the phrase being similar to the saying <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ ضَلَّ سَعْيُكَ</foreign> [expl. above]. wherefore it may be used of him who commits any mistake whatever, and is imputed to prophets and to unbelievers, though between the <foreign lang="ar">ضلال</foreign> of the former and that of the latter is a wide difference: and in another point of view, it is of two sorts; one is in the speculative departments of knowledge, as in acquaintance with the unity of God, and with the prophetic function or office, and the like, indicated in the Kur iv. 135; or it is in the practical departments of knowledge, as in acquaintance with the ordinances of the law, that is, religious services.
